| Split Squat | Gluteus maximus, Quadriceps femoris (rectus femoris, vastus lateralis, vastus medialis, vastus intermedius) | Hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus), gluteus medius, erector spinae, gastrocnemius, soleus | Compound | Bodyweight, dumbbells, barbell, kettlebells | Intermediate | Lower | Push | Bodyweight | 1. Stand with feet hip-width apart, then step one foot forward approximately 2-3 feet (60-90cm) to create a staggered stance 2. Position your back heel elevated off the ground with weight on the ball of your foot; front foot should be flat on the floor 3. Engage your core muscles and maintain an upright torso with shoulders back and chest proud 4. Lower your body by bending both knees simultaneously until your front thigh is parallel to the ground and your back knee hovers 1-2 inches (2.5-5cm) above the floor 5. Keep your front knee aligned over your ankle without allowing it to travel past your toes 6. Push through your front heel to return to the starting position, fully extending both legs 7. Complete all repetitions on one leg before switching to the other side |  | Mackey, E. R., & Riemann, B. L. (2021). Biomechanical Differences Between the Bulgarian Split-Squat and Back Squat. | Step-Up | Gluteus maximus, quadriceps femoris (rectus femoris, vastus lateralis, vastus medialis, vastus intermedius) | Hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus), gluteus medius, gastrocnemius, soleus, erector spinae, core stabilizers | Compound | Bodyweight, dumbbells, barbell, kettlebells, box/bench/step | Beginner to Intermediate | Lower | Push | Bodyweight | 1. Stand facing a sturdy box, bench, or step that is approximately knee height (12-18 inches / 30-45cm for beginners) 2. Place your entire right foot flat on top of the box with your knee aligned over your ankle 3. Engage your core and maintain an upright posture with shoulders back and chest lifted 4. Push through your right heel to lift your body onto the box, straightening your right leg completely while bringing your left foot to meet your right foot on top of the box 5. Pause briefly at the top with both feet on the box and hips fully extended 6. Step down with your left foot first, lowering your body in a controlled manner, followed by your right foot returning to the starting position 7. Complete all repetitions leading with the right leg before switching to lead with the left leg |  | Neto, W. K., et al. (2020). | Alternating Leg Extension | Quadriceps femoris (rectus femoris, vastus lateralis, vastus medialis, vastus intermedius) | Hip flexors (iliopsoas), tibialis anterior | Isolation | Leg extension machine | Beginner to Intermediate | Lower | Extension | Bodyweight | 1. Sit on the leg extension machine and adjust the backrest so your knee joint aligns with the machine's pivot point 2. Position the shin pad against your lower shins (just above the ankles) and adjust the pad so it rests comfortably on your legs 3. Grip the handles on each side of the seat and engage your core muscles to stabilize your torso against the backrest 4. Starting with your right leg, extend your knee by contracting your quadriceps to lift the weight until your leg is fully straight (0-5° knee angle) 5. Pause briefly at the top position with your quadriceps fully contracted, then slowly lower the weight back to the starting position (90° knee flexion) over 2-3 seconds 6. Complete the full repetition with your right leg, then immediately perform the same movement with your left leg 7. Continue alternating legs for the prescribed number of repetitions per leg, maintaining controlled tempo throughout |  | Stoutenberg, M., et al. (2005). The Impact of Foot Position on Electromyographical Activity of the Superficial Quadriceps Muscles During Leg Extension. Journal of Strength and Conditioning Research, 19(4), 931-938. https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16437818/; Alkner, B. A., et al. (2000). | Leg Extension | Quadriceps femoris (rectus femoris, vastus lateralis, vastus medialis, vastus intermedius) | Hip flexors (iliopsoas), tibialis anterior | Isolation | Leg extension machine | Beginner | Lower | Extension | Bodyweight | 1. Sit on the leg extension machine and adjust the backrest so your knee joints align with the machine's pivot point 2. Position the shin pad against your lower shins just above your ankles and adjust the pad height for comfortable contact with both legs 3. Grip the handles on each side of the seat to stabilize your upper body and prevent your hips from lifting during the movement 4. Engage your core muscles and press your lower back firmly against the backrest throughout the exercise 5. Contract your quadriceps to extend both knees simultaneously, lifting the weight until your legs are fully straight (0-5° knee angle) 6. Pause for 1 second at the top position with your quadriceps fully contracted and squeeze your thigh muscles 7. Slowly lower the weight back to the starting position (approximately 90° knee flexion) over 2-3 seconds, maintaining control throughout the descent |  | Peng, H. T., et al. (2014). | Single-Leg Extension | Quadriceps femoris (rectus femoris, vastus lateralis, vastus medialis, vastus intermedius) | Hip flexors (iliopsoas), tibialis anterior, core stabilizers | Isolation | Leg extension machine | Intermediate | Lower | Extension | Bodyweight | 1. Sit on the leg extension machine and adjust the backrest so your knee joint aligns with the machine's pivot point 2. Position the shin pad against your lower shin (just above the ankle) on your working leg; rest your non-working leg on the floor or slightly elevated 3. Grip the handles on each side of the seat firmly to stabilize your torso and prevent hip rotation during the movement 4. Engage your core muscles and maintain neutral spine alignment by pressing your lower back against the backrest 5. Contract your quadriceps to extend your knee, lifting the weight until your leg is fully straight (0-5° knee angle) 6. Pause for 1-2 seconds at the top position with your quadriceps fully contracted and actively squeeze your thigh muscles 7. Slowly lower the weight back to the starting position (approximately 90° knee flexion) over 3-4 seconds, maintaining complete control throughout the eccentric phase |  | Cronin, J., et al. (2019). | Alternating Superman | Erector spinae (iliocostalis, longissimus, spinalis), multifidus | Gluteus maximus, hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus), posterior deltoids, rhomboids, trapezius (lower and middle fibers) | Isolation/Stabilization | Bodyweight, exercise mat | Beginner to Intermediate | Core | Static | Bodyweight | 1. Lie face down (prone) on an exercise mat with your legs extended straight behind you and arms extended straight overhead 2. Position your forehead on the mat or turn your head to one side for comfort; engage your core muscles by drawing your navel toward your spine 3. Simultaneously lift your right arm and left leg off the mat by 6-12 inches (15-30cm) while keeping both limbs straight and fully extended 4. Squeeze your right shoulder blade toward your spine and contract your left glute and hamstring to lift your leg; hold this position for 2-3 seconds 5. Slowly lower your right arm and left leg back to the starting position in a controlled manner 6. Immediately lift your left arm and right leg off the mat using the same technique, holding for 2-3 seconds at the top 7. Continue alternating sides for the prescribed number of repetitions, maintaining controlled movement throughout and breathing steadily |  | McGill, S. M., et al. (2009). Journal of Strength and Conditioning Research, 23(4), 1148-1161. https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC5435978/; Youdas, J. W., et al. (2017). | Back Raise | Erector spinae (iliocostalis, longissimus, spinalis), multifidus | Gluteus maximus, hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus) | Compound | 45-degree hyperextension bench (Roman chair), weight plates (optional), barbell (optional) | Intermediate | Core | Isolation | Bodyweight | 1. Position yourself on a 45-degree hyperextension bench with your hips resting on the padded support and your ankles secured under the ankle pads 2. Adjust the pad height so the front edge sits at the crease of your hips, allowing full range of motion without restricting movement 3. Cross your arms across your chest or place your hands behind your head (easier variation: arms crossed; harder variation: hands behind head) 4. Begin with your torso perpendicular to your legs (approximately 90° hip flexion), creating a right angle at your hips 5. Engage your core, squeeze your glutes, and slowly raise your torso by extending at the hips and spine until your body forms a straight line from head to heels 6. Pause for 1-2 seconds at the top position with your glutes and erector spinae fully contracted 7. Slowly lower your torso back to the starting position over 3-4 seconds, maintaining control throughout the descent; avoid excessive spinal flexion at bottom position |  | Leighton, D., et al. (2021). Comparison of Muscle Activity in Three Single-Joint, Hip Extension Exercises in Resistance-Trained Women. Journal of Strength and Conditioning Research, 33(8), 2053-2056. https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/30946266/; Youdas, J. W., et al. (2003). | Quadruped Alternating Superman | Erector spinae (iliocostalis, longissimus, spinalis), multifidus, transverse abdominis, internal obliques | Gluteus maximus, gluteus medius, posterior deltoids, rhomboids, trapezius (lower and middle), hip flexors (iliopsoas) | Stabilization/Core | Bodyweight, exercise mat | Beginner to Intermediate | Lower | Static | Bodyweight | 1. Begin on your hands and knees (quadruped position) with hands directly under shoulders and knees directly under hips on an exercise mat 2. Establish neutral spine alignment with your head, spine, and pelvis in a straight line; engage your core by drawing your navel toward your spine 3. Simultaneously extend your right arm straight forward (parallel to the ground) and your left leg straight back (parallel to the ground) 4. Ensure your extended arm and leg form a straight line with your torso; your right hand should reach forward and your left foot should flex with toes pointing down 5. Hold this position for 3-5 seconds while maintaining neutral spine, avoiding any rotation, sagging, or arching of your lower back 6. Slowly return your right hand and left knee to the starting position in a controlled manner 7. Immediately repeat the movement on the opposite side (left arm and right leg), alternating sides for the prescribed number of repetitions |  | Calatayud, J., et al. (2023). Electromyographic and Stabilometric Analysis of the Static and Dynamic "Standing Bird Dog" Exercise. Sports, 11(6), 119. https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10305076/; Park, K. N., et al. (2022). Can Knee Joint Flexion Position of the Raised Lower Limb Affect Trunk Muscle Activation During Bird Dog Exercise in Subjects With Chronic Low Back Pain? | Superman | Erector spinae (iliocostalis, longissimus, spinalis), multifidus | Gluteus maximus, hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus), posterior deltoids, rhomboids, trapezius (lower and middle), splenius | Isolation/Stabilization | Bodyweight, exercise mat | Beginner | Core | Static | Bodyweight | 1. Lie face down (prone) on an exercise mat with your legs extended straight and your arms extended straight overhead, palms facing down 2. Position your forehead on the mat or turn your head to one side for comfort; engage your core by drawing your navel toward your spine 3. Simultaneously lift both arms, chest, and both legs off the mat by 6-12 inches (15-30cm), creating a gentle arch in your back 4. Keep all four limbs straight and fully extended while lifting; focus on lengthening your body rather than just lifting higher 5. Squeeze your shoulder blades together, contract your glutes and hamstrings, and engage your lower back muscles 6. Hold this extended position for 5-10 seconds while breathing steadily (avoid holding your breath) 7. Slowly lower all limbs back to the starting position in a controlled manner and rest briefly before repeating |  | Kang, S. Y., et al. (2022). | Superman Hold | Erector spinae (iliocostalis, longissimus, spinalis), multifidus | Gluteus maximus, hamstrings (biceps femoris, semitendinosus, semimembranosus), posterior deltoids, rhomboids, trapezius (lower and middle), splenius, anterior deltoids, lateral deltoids | Isometric/Stabilization | Bodyweight, exercise mat | Intermediate to Advanced | Core | Static | Bodyweight | 1. Lie face down (prone) on an exercise mat with your legs extended straight and your arms extended straight overhead, palms facing down or toward each other 2. Position your forehead lightly on the mat initially; engage your core muscles by drawing your navel toward your spine 3. Simultaneously lift both arms, chest, and both legs off the mat by 6-12 inches (15-30cm), creating a gentle controlled arch in your back 4. Keep all four limbs straight and fully extended; focus on lengthening your body from fingertips to toes rather than just lifting higher 5. Squeeze your shoulder blades together, contract your glutes and hamstrings firmly, and engage your lower back muscles (erector spinae) 6. Hold this extended position for 20-30 seconds initially (beginners) or 45-60+ seconds (advanced) while breathing steadily through your nose and mouth 7. Slowly lower all limbs back to the starting position in a controlled manner; rest for 30-60 seconds before performing additional holds |  | Kang, S. Y., et al. (2022). | Barbell Shoulder Press | Deltoideus (anterior and lateral heads) | Deltoideus (posterior head), triceps brachii (all heads), trapezius (upper and middle fibers), serratus anterior, rotator cuff (supraspinatus, infraspinatus, subscapularis, teres minor), core muscles (rectus abdominis, external obliques, erector spinae) | Compound | Barbell, squat rack or power rack | Intermediate | Upper | Push | Free Weight | 1. Stand with feet shoulder-width apart, barbell racked at upper chest level, grip bar slightly wider than shoulder width with full grip (thumbs around bar) 2. Position barbell on anterior deltoids/upper chest with elbows slightly forward of bar, wrists neutral (straight line from elbow through knuckles) 3. Unrack bar and step back, establish stable stance with slight knee flexion, engage core by bracing as if preparing for punch to stomach 4. Take deep breath and hold (Valsalva maneuver), press bar vertically upward, moving head back slightly to allow bar path past face 5. Continue pressing until arms reach full extension with bar directly over shoulders and mid-foot, elbows fully locked but not hyperextended 6. Lower bar under control along same vertical path to starting position at upper chest/clavicle level, exhale during descent 7. Reset breathing and position between repetitions, complete 5-8 repetitions with strict form before fatigue compromises technique |  | Kruszczyński, K., Stastny, P., & Golas, A. (2022). | Dumbbell Front Raise | Deltoideus (anterior head - clavicular portion) | Deltoideus (lateral head), pectoralis major (clavicular head), serratus anterior, trapezius (upper fibers), biceps brachii (short head), coracobrachialis | Isolation | Dumbbells (or single barbell, cable, plate) | Beginner to Intermediate | Upper | Isolation | Free Weight | 1. Stand with feet shoulder-width apart, knees slightly flexed, hold dumbbells in front of thighs with arms fully extended and slight elbow bend (10-15°) 2. Position dumbbells with pronated grip (palms facing down/toward thighs), wrists neutral, dumbbells approximately 2-3 inches apart or touching 3. Engage core muscles, maintain neutral spine with shoulders retracted and depressed (down and back), chest up position 4. Raise dumbbells forward and upward along arc in sagittal plane, keeping arms parallel to each other, maintain slight elbow bend throughout 5. Continue raising until dumbbells reach eye level or shoulder height (90° shoulder flexion), pause briefly at top of movement (1 second) 6. Lower dumbbells slowly and under control along same arc path back to starting position at thighs, resisting gravity throughout eccentric phase 7. Avoid swinging or using momentum, complete 10-15 repetitions with strict form, using 2-3 second eccentric (lowering) phase for maximum muscle tension |  | Campos, Y. A. C., Vianna, J. | Smith Machine Shoulder Press | Deltoideus (anterior and lateral heads) | Deltoideus (posterior head), triceps brachii (all heads), trapezius (upper fibers), serratus anterior | Compound | Smith machine | Beginner to Intermediate | Upper | Push | Machine | 1. Adjust bar height so it begins at upper chest/clavicle level when seated or standing, position bench inside Smith machine if using seated variation 2. Sit or stand with bar positioned at front of shoulders, grip bar slightly wider than shoulder width with pronated grip (palms forward) 3. Position hands symmetrically on bar, wrists neutral (stacked under elbows), elbows pointing forward and slightly downward at start position 4. Engage core by bracing midsection, maintain neutral spine with shoulder blades retracted, unrack bar by rotating hooks off catches 5. Press bar straight upward along fixed vertical path until arms reach full extension, elbows locked but not hyperextended 6. Pause briefly at top position (1 second), maintaining full-body tension and shoulder stability 7. Lower bar under control along same vertical path back to starting position at upper chest, complete 8-12 repetitions before re-racking on catches |  | Schwanbeck, S., Chilibeck, P. D., & Binsted, G. (2009). A comparison of free weight squat to Smith machine squat using electromyography. | Barbell Front Raise | Deltoideus (anterior head - clavicular portion) | Deltoideus (lateral head), pectoralis major (clavicular head), serratus anterior, trapezius (upper fibers), core stabilizers (rectus abdominis, external obliques - standing variation) | Isolation | Barbell (straight or EZ-curl bar), weight plates | Intermediate | Upper | Isolation | Free Weight | 1. Stand with feet shoulder-width apart, knees slightly flexed, hold barbell with pronated grip (palms facing down) at hip level, hands shoulder-width apart 2. Position barbell resting against front of thighs, arms fully extended with slight elbow bend (10-15°), wrists neutral 3. Engage core muscles, establish neutral spine with shoulders retracted and depressed, chest up position 4. Raise barbell forward and upward along arc in sagittal plane, keeping arms parallel and maintaining slight elbow bend throughout 5. Continue raising until barbell reaches eye level or shoulder height (90° shoulder flexion), barbell should be 8-12 inches in front of face at top 6. Pause briefly at top position (1 second), squeeze anterior deltoids consciously 7. Lower barbell slowly and under control along same arc path back to starting position at thighs, avoid dropping weight or using momentum for 10-12 repetitions |  | Campos, Y. A. C., Vianna, J. M., Guimarães, M. P., Oliveira, J. L. D., Hernández-Mosqueira, C., da Silva, S. F., & Marchetti, P. H. (2020). | Bent-Over Cable Rear Delt Raise | Deltoideus (posterior head) | Rhomboideus major and minor, trapezius (middle fibers), infraspinatus, teres minor, teres major | Isolation | Cable machine with single-handle attachments or rope | Intermediate | Upper | Isolation | Cables | 1. Set cable pulleys at shoulder height, attach single-handle or D-handle to each side, stand centered between pulleys with feet shoulder-width apart 2. Reach across body with right hand to grab left cable handle and left hand to grab right cable handle (arms crossed), step back to create tension 3. Hinge forward at hips 60-70°, knees slightly bent, maintain neutral spine with chest lifted, let arms hang crossed in front of chest with slight elbow bend 4. Pull both handles outward and backward (transverse extension) along horizontal plane, leading with elbows rather than hands 5. Continue pulling until arms are perpendicular to torso or slightly behind body, upper arms aligned with shoulders in transverse plane 6. Squeeze shoulder blades together at peak contraction, focusing on posterior deltoid engagement for 1-2 seconds 7. Return cables to starting position with controlled eccentric motion, maintaining torso position and constant tension, complete 12-15 repetitions |  | Campos, Y. A. C., Vianna, J. M., Guimarães, M. P., Oliveira, J. L. D., Hernández-Mosqueira, C., da Silva, S. F., & Marchetti, P. H. (2020). Different Shoulder Exercises Affect the Activation of Deltoid Portions in Resistance-Trained Individuals. | Bent-Over Dumbbell Rear Delt Raise | Deltoideus (posterior head) | Rhomboideus major and minor, trapezius (middle fibers), infraspinatus, teres minor, teres major, latissimus dorsi (upper fibers) | Isolation | Dumbbells, bench (optional for chest-supported variation) | Beginner to Intermediate | Upper | Isolation | Free Weight | 1. Stand with feet hip-width apart, hold dumbbells with neutral grip (palms facing each other), hinge forward at hips until torso reaches 60-70° angle 2. Let arms hang straight down toward floor beneath shoulders with slight elbow bend (10-20°), maintain neutral spine with natural lumbar curve 3. Engage core muscles to support torso position, keep chest lifted and shoulder blades retracted, avoid rounding upper back 4. Raise dumbbells outward and upward in wide arc, leading movement with elbows rather than hands, maintain slight elbow bend throughout 5. Continue raising until upper arms are parallel to floor or slightly above, arms perpendicular to torso in transverse plane 6. Squeeze shoulder blades together at top of movement, pause for 1-2 seconds while consciously contracting posterior deltoids 7. Lower dumbbells slowly and under control back to starting position, maintain torso angle throughout set, complete 12-15 repetitions with 2-3 second eccentric |  | ACE (American Council on Exercise). | Cable Front Raise | Deltoideus (anterior head - clavicular portion) | Deltoideus (lateral head), pectoralis major (clavicular head), serratus anterior, trapezius (upper fibers), core stabilizers (anti-extension) | Isolation | Cable machine with straight bar, rope, or single-handle attachments | Beginner to Intermediate | Upper | Isolation | Cables | 1. Set cable pulley to lowest position, attach straight bar or rope, stand facing away from machine with feet shoulder-width apart 2. Grip bar with pronated grip (palms down) or rope with neutral grip, position hands shoulder-width apart, start with cable behind legs creating tension 3. Step forward 1-2 feet from machine to create starting tension, arms extended with slight elbow bend (10-15°), bar positioned against front of thighs 4. Engage core muscles, establish neutral spine with shoulders retracted and depressed, chest up position to resist forward cable pull 5. Raise bar or rope forward and upward along arc in sagittal plane, maintaining slight elbow bend and parallel arm position throughout 6. Continue raising until bar reaches eye level or shoulder height (90° shoulder flexion), maintaining constant tension from cable throughout ascent 7. Pause briefly at top (1 second), slowly lower bar back to starting position with controlled eccentric (2-3 seconds), resisting cable tension throughout descent for 12-15 repetitions |  | Campos, Y. A. C., Vianna, J. M., Guimarães, M. P., Oliveira, J. L. D., Hernández-Mosqueira, C., da Silva, S. F., & Marchetti, P. H. (2020).
